2024-06-28T18:43:41.5875367Z (Linux, Mac OS X, Windows, Cygwin, Windows CE, and Symbian). Based
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5876878Z on the xUnit architecture. Supports automatic test discovery, a rich
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5878824Z set of assertions, user-defined assertions, death tests, fatal and

2024-06-28T18:43:41.5885500Z and map and transform structured data with the same ease that

2024-06-28T18:43:41.5887584Z This is a line-editing library. It can be linked into almost

2024-06-28T18:43:41.5892426Z lowdown is a Markdown translator producing HTML5 and roff documents in
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5893412Z the ms and man formats. It's just clean, secure, open source C code with
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5894232Z no dependencies. Its canonical documentation is lowdown(1) for the
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5894956Z formatter, lowdown(5) for the syntax, and the library interface at
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5895701Z lowdown(3).
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5895986Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5896255Z lowdown started as a fork of hoedown to add sandboxing (pledge(2),
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5896995Z capsicum(4), or sandbox_init(3)) and roff output to securely generate
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5897684Z PDFs on OpenBSD with just mandoc(1).
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5898003Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5898579Z It has grown to admit many more extensions and outputs, and can even be
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5899373Z used to show the difference between two Markdown documents with
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5900537Z lowdown-diff, documented as the lowdown diffing engine. This uses a
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5901407Z tree-based difference algorithm to show semantically-valid Markdown
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5902072Z differences.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5902525Z lowdown added to install queue.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5902836Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5902997Z libcpuid (library for x86 CPU detection)
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5903330Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5903721Z libcpuid is a small C library for x86 CPU detection and feature
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5904438Z extraction.  Using it, you can:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5904683Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5904964Z * get the processor vendor, model, brand string, code name
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5905665Z * get information about CPU features such as: number of cores or logical
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5906391Z   CPUs, cache sizes, CPU clock
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5906990Z * check if the processor implements a specific instruction set such as
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5907640Z   SSE2 or 3DNow!
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5908179Z * execute the CPUID and RDTSC instructions (portably!)
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5908827Z * and have this all in your commercial application, without getting into
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5909484Z   trouble.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5909640Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5910232Z It works on Windows, Linux and Mac OS X, both 32-bit and 64-bit
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5911017Z flavours. Compiler support includes GCC and Microsoft Visual C++ (and
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5911730Z compatible, e.g. Intel C++ compiler).
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5912258Z libcpuid added to install queue.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5912637Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5912903Z There are myriads of JSON libraries out there, and each may even have
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5913620Z its reason to exist. Our class had these design goals:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5914101Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5914379Z Intuitive syntax. In languages such as Python, JSON feels like a first
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5915382Z class data type. We used all the operator magic of modern C++ to achieve
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5916325Z the same feeling in your code. Check out the examples below and you'll
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5917022Z know what I mean.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5917330Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5917600Z Trivial integration. Our whole code consists of a single header file
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5918417Z json.hpp. That's it. No library, no subproject, no dependencies, no
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5919301Z complex build system. The class is written in vanilla C++11. All in all,
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5920077Z everything should require no adjustment of your compiler flags or
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5920626Z project settings.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5920969Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5921353Z Serious testing. Our class is heavily unit-tested and covers 100% of the
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5922023Z code, including all exceptional behavior. Furthermore, we checked with
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5922820Z Valgrind and the Clang Sanitizers that there are no memory leaks. Google
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5923632Z OSS-Fuzz additionally runs fuzz tests against all parsers 24/7,
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5924265Z effectively executing billions of tests so far. To maintain high
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5925011Z quality, the project is following the Core Infrastructure Initiative
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5925621Z (CII) best practices.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5925813Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5926006Z Other aspects were not so important to us:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5926297Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5926561Z Memory efficiency. Each JSON object has an overhead of one pointer (the
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5927292Z maximal size of a union) and one enumeration element (1 byte). The
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5928007Z default generalization uses the following C++ data types: std::string
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5928772Z for strings, int64_t, uint64_t or double for numbers, std::map for
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5929523Z objects, std::vector for arrays, and bool for Booleans. However, you can
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5930162Z template the generalized class basic_json to your needs.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5930494Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5930760Z Speed. There are certainly faster JSON libraries out there. However, if
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5932287Z your goal is to speed up your development by adding JSON support with a
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5933334Z single header, then this library is the way to go. If you know how to
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5933912Z use a std::vector or std::map, you are already set.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5934507Z nlohmann_json added to install queue.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5934814Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5934955Z nix (functional package manager)
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5935272Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5935678Z Nix is a purely functional package manager. This means that it treats
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5936339Z packages like values in purely functional programming languages
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5937064Z such as Haskell -- they are built by functions that don't have
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5937812Z side-effects, and they never change after they have been built. Nix
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5938750Z stores packages in the Nix store, usually the directory /nix/store,
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5939382Z where each package has its own unique subdirectory such as
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5939722Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5940161Z     /nix/store/b6gvzjyb2pg0kjfwrjmg1vfhh54ad73z-firefox-33.1/
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5940541Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5940841Z where b6gvzjyb2pg0... is a unique identifier for the package that
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5941694Z captures all its dependencies (it's a cryptographic hash of the
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5942856Z package's build dependency graph).
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5943159Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5943494Z Nix may be run in single or multi-user mode (which requires the
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5944085Z nix-daemon).  The following sets up multi-user mode.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5944504Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5944894Z To have the nix daemon start and stop with your host, add to
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5945459Z /etc/rc.d/rc.local:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5945643Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5945824Z     if [ -x /etc/rc.d/rc.nix ]; then
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5946501Z       /etc/rc.d/rc.nix start
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5946876Z     fi
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5947020Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5947243Z and to /etc/rc.d/rc.local_shutdown (creating it if needed):
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5947710Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5948135Z     if [ -x /etc/rc.d/rc.nix ]; then
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5948780Z       /etc/rc.d/rc.nix stop
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5949277Z     fi
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5949579Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5950657Z The daemon requires users for building the nix packages, which should
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5951742Z be added under the 'nixbld' group.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5952204Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5952576Z     # groupadd -g 314 nixbld
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5953584Z     # for n in $(seq 1 10); do useradd -c "Nix build user $n" \
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5954662Z     #     -d /var/empty -g nixbld -G nixbld -M -N -r -s /sbin/nologin \
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5955530Z     #     nixbld$n; done
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5955806Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5956158Z Restricting access to the daemon is acheived by setting file
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5956786Z permissions for the daemon's socket's folder.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5957085Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5957293Z     # groupadd nix-users
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5957774Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/daemon-socket
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5958299Z     # chmod ug=rwx,o= /nix/var/nix/daemon-socket
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5958580Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5958866Z Correct permissions must also be set for the following profile
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5959421Z directories to give users access.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5959704Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5959903Z     # mkdir -p /nix/var/nix/profiles/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5960459Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/profiles/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5961053Z     # chmod go+wt /nix/var/nix/profiles/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5961340Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5961533Z     # mkdir -p /nix/var/nix/gcroots/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5962063Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/gcroots/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5962658Z     # chmod go+wt /nix/var/nix/gcroots/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5962941Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5963777Z To setup a user to use nix, add him to the nix-users group and load
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5964357Z these lines on login (via $HOME/.profile):
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5964632Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5964877Z     export NIX_REMOTE=daemon
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5965250Z     source /etc/profile.d/nix.sh
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5965526Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5965768Z If you have patches email me, or send a pull request via github:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5966134Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5966461Z     https://github.com/PragmaticCypher/nix.SlackBuild
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5966797Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5966802Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5967139Z It looks like this slackbuild requires the following command(s) to be run first:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5967732Z     # groupadd -g 314 nixbld
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5968215Z     # groupadd nix-users
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5968476Z

2024-06-28T18:43:41.5983646Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5983912Z The daemon requires users for building the nix packages, which should
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5984596Z be added under the 'nixbld' group.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5984879Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5985046Z     # groupadd -g 314 nixbld
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5985623Z     # for n in $(seq 1 10); do useradd -c "Nix build user $n" \
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5986263Z     #     -d /var/empty -g nixbld -G nixbld -M -N -r -s /sbin/nologin \
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5986773Z     #     nixbld$n; done
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5986974Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5987311Z Restricting access to the daemon is acheived by setting file
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5987867Z permissions for the daemon's socket's folder.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5988190Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5988344Z     # groupadd nix-users
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5988866Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/daemon-socket
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5989360Z     # chmod ug=rwx,o= /nix/var/nix/daemon-socket
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5989719Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5989956Z Correct permissions must also be set for the following profile
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5990564Z directories to give users access.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5990807Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5991046Z     # mkdir -p /nix/var/nix/profiles/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5991586Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/profiles/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5992384Z     # chmod go+wt /nix/var/nix/profiles/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5992673Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5992903Z     # mkdir -p /nix/var/nix/gcroots/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5993399Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/gcroots/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5993994Z     # chmod go+wt /nix/var/nix/gcroots/per-user
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5994277Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5994611Z To setup a user to use nix, add him to the nix-users group and load
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5995157Z these lines on login (via $HOME/.profile):
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5995467Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5995662Z     export NIX_REMOTE=daemon
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5996078Z     source /etc/profile.d/nix.sh
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5996325Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5996563Z If you have patches email me, or send a pull request via github:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5996962Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5997227Z     https://github.com/PragmaticCypher/nix.SlackBuild
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5997550Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5997590Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5997735Z nix (functional package manager)
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5997983Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5998277Z Nix is a purely functional package manager. This means that it treats
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5998961Z packages like values in purely functional programming languages
2024-06-28T18:43:41.5999648Z such as Haskell -- they are built by functions that don't have
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6000328Z side-effects, and they never change after they have been built. Nix
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6001015Z stores packages in the Nix store, usually the directory /nix/store,
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6001656Z where each package has its own unique subdirectory such as
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6001995Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6002338Z     /nix/store/b6gvzjyb2pg0kjfwrjmg1vfhh54ad73z-firefox-33.1/
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6002716Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6003026Z where b6gvzjyb2pg0... is a unique identifier for the package that
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6003882Z captures all its dependencies (it's a cryptographic hash of the
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6004461Z package's build dependency graph).
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6004714Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6005119Z Nix may be run in single or multi-user mode (which requires the
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6005708Z nix-daemon).  The following sets up multi-user mode.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6006054Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6006277Z To have the nix daemon start and stop with your host, add to
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6006847Z /etc/rc.d/rc.local:
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6007029Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6007198Z     if [ -x /etc/rc.d/rc.nix ]; then
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6007598Z       /etc/rc.d/rc.nix start
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6008028Z     fi
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6008175Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6008396Z and to /etc/rc.d/rc.local_shutdown (creating it if needed):
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6008766Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6008933Z     if [ -x /etc/rc.d/rc.nix ]; then
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6009443Z       /etc/rc.d/rc.nix stop
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6009751Z     fi
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6009927Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6010203Z The daemon requires users for building the nix packages, which should
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6010878Z be added under the 'nixbld' group.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6011126Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6011316Z     # groupadd -g 314 nixbld
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6011797Z     # for n in $(seq 1 10); do useradd -c "Nix build user $n" \
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6012521Z     #     -d /var/empty -g nixbld -G nixbld -M -N -r -s /sbin/nologin \
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6013030Z     #     nixbld$n; done
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6013227Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6013466Z Restricting access to the daemon is acheived by setting file
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6014129Z permissions for the daemon's socket's folder.
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6014423Z 
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6014611Z     # groupadd nix-users
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6015031Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/daemon-socket
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6015656Z     # chmod ug=rwx,o= /nix/var/nix/daemon-socket
2024-06-28T18:43:41.6015948Z

2024-06-28T18:43:41.6017198Z

2024-06-28T18:43:41.6017951Z     # chgrp nix-users /nix/var/nix/profiles/per-user
